Crimes -- possession of blank cartridge pistol -- City Court dismissed information which charged defendant with violation of section 270.00 (subd 2) of Penal Law, based on his possession of blank cartridge pistol, upon ground that, insofar as it related to blank cartridge pistols, statute was unconstitutionally vague -- County Court reversed and reinstated  [**2] information, concluding that statute was constitutional -- order of County Court affirmed. 

 

38 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fonseca


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


36 N.Y.2d 133; 325 N.E.2d 143; 365 N.Y.S.2d 818; 1975 N.Y. LEXIS 1722


January 15, 1975, Argued  
February 19, 1975, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed defendant's convictions for criminal possession of stolen property in the second degree, assault in the second degree, unauthorized use of a vehicle, and possession of a dangerous instrument.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal possession of stolen property in the second degree, assault in the second degree, unauthorized use of a vehicle, and possession of a dangerous instrument. Defendant, while driving a stolen automobile and being pursued by police, struck a taxicab, injuring two people. Defendant claimed that the charge of criminal possession of stolen property could not serve as the basis for a charge of felony assault, pursuant to N.Y. Penal Law § 120.05(6). Defendant asserted that the felony assault statute was directed at dangerous felonies only. The intermediate and appellate courts both disagreed and affirmed defendant's convictions. The appellate court said that the New York legislature did not intend the felony assault statute to be directed only at a certain class of felonious behavior.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for criminal possession of stolen property in the second degree, assault in the second degree, unauthorized use of a vehicle, and possession of a dangerous instrument. The court rejected defendant's argument that the legislature intended the felony assault charge to be based solely upon dangerous underlying felonies.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- assault -- Penal Law ( § 120.05, subd. 6) provides that person is guilty of assault in second degree when, in course of and in furtherance of commission or attempted commission of felony, he causes physical injury to person other than participant -- defendant, while in possession of stolen automobile struck taxicab, injuring two of its occupants -- felony of criminal possession of stolen property properly served as predicate for felony assault conviction -- Legislature did not intend to limit such predicate felonies to dangerous felonies.

1. The Penal Law ( § 120.05, subd. 6) provides that: "A person is guilty of assault in the second degree when: * * * In the course of and in furtherance of the commission or attempted commission of a felony * * * he, or another participant if there be any, causes physical injury to a person other than one of the participants." Defendant, while in possession of a stolen automobile struck a taxicab, injuring two occupants of the taxicab. The felony of criminal possession of stolen property properly served as a predicate for a felony assault conviction pursuant to the statute.

2. The Legislature in enacting the felony assault provision did not intend to limit to dangerous felonies the predicate felonies giving rise to felony assault in the same manner as it had limited the predicate felonies for felony murder. The language of the statute is clear and unambiguous, and does not specify that only felonies of a violent nature may be the basis for a felony assault conviction.

3. The statute does not conclusively presume an intention to cause physical injury or that the possibility of physical injury can be foreseen. Rather it is constructive malice that is ascribed. Due process does not preclude a legislative policy determination that the felon who proximately causes injury to another, irrespective of the nature of the underlying felonious act, may be held criminally accountable.

4. An alleged error in submitting to the jury criminal possession of stolen property in the second degree and unauthorized use of a vehicle has not been preserved for review in this court.

 

39 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Kleinfeldt v. New York City Employees' Retirement System


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


36 N.Y.2d 95; 324 N.E.2d 865; 365 N.Y.S.2d 500; 1975 N.Y. LEXIS 1654; 89 L.R.R.M. 2209


January 13, 1975, Argued  
February 18, 1975, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, without costs, in accordance with the opinion herein [**2] and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, public retirement system and state official, challenged a decision from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed an order of the trial court granting summary judgment to respondent retired public employee and declaring unconstitutional the retroactive application of N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 431.


OVERVIEW: Section 431 limited the amount of increased compensation that could be considered in determining the final average salary for retirement purposes of public employees. The retired individual filed a class action challenging the constitutionality of the retroactive application of the statute to himself and others similarly situated. The trial court granted him summary judgement. The appellate court affirmed, and on appeal, the court modified and affirmed. The court held that the retroactive application of the statute diminished or impaired the benefits of membership in the retirement system in violation of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 7. The court modified the order to state that it was the effective date of the statute, rather than the operative date, that controlled the constitutional reach of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court modified and affirmed the decision, which affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to the retired individual against the retirement system and the state official.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- retirement  -- retroactive application of section 431 (subd. 4) of Retirement and Social Security Law, which limits amount of increased compensation to be considered in computation of final average salary for pension purposes, to members of retirement system before its effective date violates Constitution (art. V, § 7); such application constitutes diminution and impairment of membership benefits -- date from which retroactivity should be determined is effective date, not operative date, of statute.

1. Subdivision 4 of section 431 of the Retirement and Social Security Law limits the amount of increased compensation which may be considered in the computation of the final average salary of a civil service employee for pension purposes to a maximum of 20% over the previous year. The retroactive application of that statute to those who became members of a public retirement system before its effective date constitutes a diminution and impairment of membership benefits in violation of section 7 of article V of the New York Constitution. An employee's rate of compensation is the most significant part of the formula for determining retirement allowances and is entitled to the protection of the Constitution. Increases in salary may not be excluded from final average salary for prior members.

2. The date from which retroactivity should be determined is June 17, 1971, the effective date (L. 1971, ch. 503, § 20) and not April 1, 1972, the operative date, of the statute.

 

40 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


First Nat'l City Bank v. New York Finance Administration


(NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL)


COURT OF APPEALS OF NEW YORK


36 N.Y.2d 87; 324 N.E.2d 861; 365 N.Y.S.2d 493; 1975 N.Y. LEXIS 1664


January 8, 1975, Argued  
February 17, 1975, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, without costs, and the matter remitted to Special Term for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent bank brought an action against appellant city to recover invalidly levied taxes. The trial court noted the availability of remedies alternative to a refund claim under the city's administrative code and denied the city's motion to dismiss for untimeliness. The Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York) affirmed the award with interest. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city claimed the refund application was untimely and that the bank could have avoided any time bar by pursuing a plenary action. The bank claimed it was not barred from pursuing a remedy in an action for moneys had and received and that the statute of limitations was tolled from the time it filed its claim under the city's administrative code and when it brought the judicial proceeding. The court held that the proceeding under the city's administrative code was untimely but that it should have been converted into a plenary action to avoid dismissal. When a tax statute was alleged to be unconstitutional, it could be challenged in judicial proceedings other than those prescribed by the statute as exclusive, and the invalidity or total inapplicability affected the entire statute, including the limitations and restrictions on the remedy provided in it. The court was empowered to convert a civil judicial proceeding not brought in the proper form into one brought in proper form rather than to grant a dismissal as to a substantial part of the relief sought. The bank's claim would be deemed interposed when the notice of petition was served and not when the refund application was filed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate division was vacated and the case remitted to the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Limitations of actions - refund of taxes - limitations contained in exclusive procedures of contested statute - unconstitutional taxing statute - tolling provisions - interest - article 78 proceeding brought pursuant to exclusive procedures of contested municipal taxing statute is subject to short Statute of Limitations contained in taxing statute - since tax statute alleged to be unconstitutional or wholly inapplicable may be challenged in judicial proceedings other than those prescribed by statute as exclusive, proceeding may be treated as plenary action for moneys had and received, for which limitations period is six years - plenary action is deemed interposed at date that special proceeding was brought, not on date that refund application was filed - city may serve answer containing Statute of Limitations - bank should be awarded 3% interest on refunded taxes.

1. More than five years after its first disputed quarterly payment of municipal taxes, the petitioner bank filed a refund claim pursuant to the exclusive procedures of the contested taxing provisions. When the greater portion of the late claim was denied, after a three-year administrative delay, as being precluded by the short Statute of Limitations prescribed by the taxing statute (Administrative Code of the City of New York, § L46-9.0), the petitioner brought this article 78 proceeding under the statute. Although the proceeding resorted to is timely to review the adverse determination, it is subject to the statutory time limit which bars a claim brought after the later of 18 months from the date for filing the tax return or 6 months from the date of payment.

2. Since a tax statute alleged to be unconstitutional or wholly inapplicable may be challenged in judicial proceedings other than those prescribed by the statute as exclusive, the proceeding may be treated under CPLR 103 (subd. [c]) as a plenary action for moneys had and received, for which the applicable limitations period is six years.

3. The plenary action is deemed to have been interposed on the date that the special proceeding was brought, not on the date that the refund application was filed, since only judicial proceedings toll the six-year Statute of Limitations, and the 30-day bar from institution of an action or proceeding after filing (Administrative Code of the City of New York, § 394a-1.0, subd. a) did not toll the statute beyond 30 days.

4. The city may serve an answer pleading, if it be so advised, the Statute of Limitations.

5. The bank should be awarded interest at 3% from the date of payment on that portion of the taxes, refund of which is not barred by the Statute of Limitations.

 

41 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Jerry v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 534; 324 N.E.2d 106; 364 N.Y.S.2d 440; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1060


October 10, 1974; November 21, 1974, Argued  
December 20, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: In each case: Order modified, without costs, in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate actions, plaintiff tenured teachers (teachers) brought an action against defendant Board of Education (Board), contending that their suspension without pay, prior to the determination of disciplinary proceedings under N.Y. Educ. Law § 3020-a, was unconstitutional. Two separate departments of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court (New York) ordered the Board to pay the teachers back and continuing pay. All parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that, as presently drafted, § 3020-a did not authorize suspension of a tenured teacher without pay. Because compensation was a matter of substantive right, the Board was prohibited from taking such away except pursuant to explicit statutory authorization. Further, the authority to withhold pay was not necessary to the achievement of the sound administration of the public school system, for which the power of suspension was granted. In its opinion, the court also surmised that it would not have been unconstitutional if § 3020-a were drafted to provide for suspension without pay, provided that the determination of the disciplinary proceedings were not unreasonably delayed. The court also rejected one teacher's claim that the charge arising from his relationship with a graduated student violated his constitutional right of privacy, because such right was not absolute. Further, it was too early in the proceedings to determine whether the relationship affected the teacher's professional performance directly, or if public notoriety of the relationship impaired his capabilities.


OUTCOME: The court modified and affirmed the orders.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- teachers -- suspension without pay -- withholding of pay during period of suspension of teacher is not authorized by section 3020-a of Education Law, since unnecessary and since pay is substantive right -- earnings from other sources may be credited against teacher's salary during suspension -- right of privacy does not preclude use of charge that male guidance counselor spent night with recent female graduate since private conduct ceases where responsibilities are impaired and inquiry into prior relationship or public notoriety should not be foreclosed -- conversion of article 78 proceeding into action for declaratory judgment is discretionary and is refused.

1. Section 3020-a of the Education Law does not authorize withholding of pay during a period of suspension of a teacher. The power of suspension is essential to sound public school administration, but withholding of pay is not necessary and compensation is such a substantive right that it may not be taken away without explicit statutory authorization, which should not be inferred from oblique statutory reference to restoration of full pay after an employee is acquitted of charges.

2. All earnings from other employment during a teacher's suspension may be credited against his entitlement to back salary.

3. The right of privacy does not preclude use of a charge against a guidance counselor that he spent the night with a recent female graduate of the school. What might otherwise be private conduct ceases to be so if it directly affects a teacher's professional responsibility or becomes the subject of public notoriety and reasonably impairs the teacher's capability to discharge his responsibilities. Foreclosure of further inquiry regarding a prior relationship or public notoriety would be inappropriate.

4. Conversion of an article 78 proceeding into an action for declaratory judgment under CPLR 103 (subd. [c]) is discretionary and is refused.

 

42 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Du Bois v. Town Bd. of New Paltz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 617; 324 N.E.2d 153; 364 N.Y.S.2d 506; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1066


November 20, 1974, Argued  
December 20, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, with costs to respondent, and case remitted to Supreme Court, Ulster County, for entry of a judgment in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual, for himself and as mayor, sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court Third Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed a judgment of the lower court dismissing appellant's petition to compel respondent Town Board to grant an exemption to village property owners from the town's levy for certain items for which N.Y. High. Law § 277 authorized an exemption.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. High. Law § 277 authorized certain towns to exempt village property lying within the town from highway taxes levied pursuant to N.Y. High. Law § 141 for expenditures for machinery, tools, and for snow removal. The town levied a highway tax for a number of expenditures, including those for which an exemption was authorized. The incorporated village , lying within the boundaries of the town, applied to the Town Board (Board) for an exemption, which was denied. Appellant filed an action to compel the Board to grant the exemption or, in the alternative, to have N.Y. High. Law § 277 declared unconstitutional. The trial court interpreted appellant's action as one for mandamus under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 and dismissed the action. The appellate court affirmed. Appellant sought review. The court characterized appellant's action as one for declaratory judgment under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 103(c). The court held that by its terms N.Y. High. Law § 277 unmistakably provided that whether to grant an exemption rested with the discretion of the town board. The court held that as so interpreted, § 277 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the appellate court and as so modified, affirmed it. The court's modification consisted of holding that exemption provision at issue did not command a town to grant an exemption to village property owners and that as so interpreted, the exemption provision was not unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- town highway tax -- legislative delegation to town, in which there is incorporated village forming separate road district, of authority to impose town highway taxes on real property within village is not unconstitutional since several legitimate purposes are served -- delegation of discretionary power to town boards to exempt properties within village from highway taxation for certain expenditures does not compel exemption and is constitutional since there is no basis to find impermissible delegation or unreasonable tax policy.

1. The Legislature's delegation to a town, in which there is an incorporated village which forms a separate road district, of authority to impose town highway taxes on real property within the village, is not unconstitutional. The State has great freedom in selecting the subjects of taxation and exemption. If there are any facts reasonably conceived to justify a classification, it must be upheld, and the present system of allocation of taxing powers serves several legitimate purposes.

2. The legislative delegation of discretionary authority to town boards, pursuant to section 277 of the Highway Law, to exempt properties within the village from town highway taxes for expenditures in subdivisions 3 and 4 of section 141 of the Highway Law does not compel exemption and is constitutional. Legislative judgment as to taxing statutes will be upheld if reasonable, and there is no sufficient basis to determine that section 277 involves either an impermissible delegation or unreasonable tax policy.

 

43 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mature Enterprises, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 520; 323 N.E.2d 704; 364 N.Y.S.2d 170; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1058


November 21, 1974, Argued  
December 20, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified and the case remitted to the Criminal Court of the City of New York, New York County, for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from an order of the Appellate Term of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed a judgment convicting defendant of obscenity in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 235.05 and imposing a fine of $ 100,000.


OVERVIEW: Defendant corporation was convicted of two counts of obscenity under N.Y. Penal Law §235.05 for showing the film "Deep Throat" at its Times Square theatre. The appeal raised two primary issues: (1) whether, under N.Y. Const. art. I, § 2, defendant was entitled to a jury trial and (2) whether the fine imposed exceeded the amount permitted by § 80.10 (1)[e]. The court held that the criminal court was not empowered to adjudge a forfeiture as an incident to conviction and that the right to a jury trial did not come into play since here the criminal proceedings were not "tantamount to forfeiture proceedings." Thus the lower court properly tried the case without a jury. Defendant was convicted of two offenses committed on two different dates. It was the profit from these offenses, from showing the film on these two dates, which had to be used in determining the maximum penalty authorized by law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction but reduced the fine on the grounds that by fining defendant the total profit made on the showing of the film, the lower court went beyond the legal maximum and penalized defendant for committing crimes which were neither charged nor proven at the trial.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- right to jury trial -- defendant corporation is not entitled to jury trial of charges of obscenity in second degree, since criminal proceedings therefor are not tantamount to forfeiture -- fine pursuant to section 80.10 of Penal Law, not exceeding double gain from offense, must be based upon offenses charged, two showings of film, not upon total showings of film over 37-week period, which showings were not basis for charges.

1. The defendant corporation was not entitled to a jury trial on charges of obscenity in the second degree in violation of section 235.05 of the Penal Law, a class A misdemeanor. Although section 410.00 of the Penal Law authorizes seizure of equipment used in the projection of pornographic films, a forfeiture thereunder requires proceedings in the Supreme Court, and the criminal court, therefore, has no power to adjudge a forfeiture as an incident to a conviction for obscenity. Since the criminal proceedings are not tantamount to forfeiture proceedings, there is no right to a jury trial under section 2 of article I of the State Constitution.

2. A fine imposed pursuant to section 80.10 of the Penal Law, of up to two times the gain from the offense, should not be based upon the total number of showings of a film and the total profit over 37 weeks, but should be based only upon the two showings which were the basis of the offenses charged.

 

44 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Rosenthal v. Harwood


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 469; 323 N.E.2d 179; 363 N.Y.S.2d 937; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1119


June 12, 1974, Argued  
December 19, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: On respondents' appeal: Order affirmed, without costs.

On petitioner's cross appeal: Appeal dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate and respondents, Chairman of the Nassau County Democratic Committee (chairman) and others, cross appealed from an order of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Second Judicial Department (New York), which reversed a judgment, in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. article 78 proceeding, dismissing the petition in part on the merits and granting the petition in part declaring an internal political party by-law invalid.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was nominated under the democratic and conservative parties for the same office of county judge in a general election. The chairman requested a renouncement of the conservative party nomination, but the candidate refused, was censured, then filed the action for declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court held that there was no justiciable controversy, and that a censure was improper. The appellate division reversed, declaring that the challenged by-law was invalid, proposing a prior decision was overruled. The court affirmed respondents' appeal, but dismissed petitioner's appeal. The censure issues were moot but the by-law issue was important to resolve. The court held that the overruled case the appellate division relied upon, was only overruled in part. The court departed from any holding of unlimited validity of a similar by-law and to the extent that the overruled case could have been understood to uphold the rule as to judicial candidates, but only to that extent, it was overruled. The court concluded that an internal rule or by-law of a political party was invalid if it mandated unethical conduct on the part of a candidate for judicial office.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appeal of the chairman and others and dismissed the appeal of the candidate, concluding that the internal political party by-law was invalid because it mandated unethical conduct on the part of a candidate for judicial office. The candidate brought the action for declaratory and injunctive relief but the election was over.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- rule against candidate accepting nomination of other party -- as applied to candidate for judicial office, by-laws of Nassau County Democratic Committee limiting nominations to candidates agreeing to refuse to accept nomination of any other party is invalid as contravening public policy which mandates that selection for judicial office be free from political manipulation -- although general election for which petitioner was nominated for office of County Judge is over, issue involves questions of public importance likely to arise again and will be determined -- questions raised by petitioner as to his censure by committee for accepting nomination of Conservative Party are not only moot but are not properly before court.

1. As applied to a candidate for judicial office, article VII (§ 1, subd. [f]) of the by-laws of the Nassau County Democratic Committee, limiting nominations by that party to candidates who have agreed to refuse to accept the nomination of any other political party or independent body, except a Republican nomination, is invalid as contravening public policy which mandates that selection for and performance in judicial office shall be free from political manipulation insofar as practicable. Candidates for judicial office may not indorse one another, may not attack one another and may not indorse or attack candidates for nonjudicial office. They are to be as nonpartisan as the selection of Judges by election permits. Such a by-law would compel a judicial candidate to take a partisan position not essential to his candidacy and would require unethical conduct. ( Matter of Yevoli v. Cristenfeld, 29 N Y 2d 591, overruled in part.)

2. Although the 1973 general election for which petitioner was nominated to run by the Nassau County Democratic Committee as a candidate for the office of County Judge is over and this proceeding could be said to be moot, the issue involves questions of public importance likely to arise again and, accordingly, will be determined.

3. The questions raised by petitioner as to his censure by the committee for accepting the nomination of the Conservative Party are not only moot, but are not properly before the court. The dissent at the Appellate Division was not in his favor and he was not aggrieved by the modification of the majority. Consequently, petitioner's cross appeal should be dismissed.

 

45 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Sanford v. Rockefeller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 547; 324 N.E.2d 113; 364 N.Y.S.2d 450; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1121; 88 L.R.R.M. 2189



December 19, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: October 9, 1974, Reargued



DISPOSITION: In Matter of Sanford, Matter of Splatt and Matter of Winkowski: Upon reargument: Order affirmed, without costs.

In Matter of Godbee and Matter of Collins: Upon reargument: Order affirmed, without costs. Question certified answered in the affirmative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs state employees brought an action that complained that the imposition of the Taylor Law, N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law, § 210, and subd. 2, which penalized state employees for strikes, and violated their due process rights. The United States Supreme Court vacated an opinion determining that the procedures were proper so that the court could consider the impact of another case.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs state employees brought an action that complained that the imposition of the Taylor Law, N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law, § 210, and subd. 2, which penalized state employees for strikes and violated their due process rights. The court affirmed the trial court decision that the application of the penalties was proper, but the United States Supreme Court vacated that opinion so that the court could consider the impact of a newly decided case. The court affirmed its earlier decision and determined that the case was different because the case involved fines and loss of tenure for strike activity rather than removal of non-probationary employees from the federal service and for the remedies available to the employee to contest such removal. The court concluded that the state application of the remedy did not require a pre-penalty administrative proceeding because N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 210, and subd. 2 allowed direct and adequate judicial review of the administrative determinations and the penalties of fines and loss of tenure were not severe and were reversible in both monetary terms and in status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that the Taylor Law did not deprive plaintiff state employees of due process by not allowing a pre-penalty administrative hearing for penalties in a strike because the court determined that the right to judicial review of a decision was adequate and the United States Supreme Court case requiring a hearing before termination of a tenured federal employee was not similar to the state employee strike case.


HEADNOTES

Civil service -- Public Employees' Fair Employment Act -- penalties on employees for strikes -- constitutional due process is satisfied by statutory procedures (Civil Service Law, art. 14, § 210) and by judicial reviewability under CPLR article 78.

1. When the State of New York and the Civil Service Employees Association failed to reach an agreement on the terms of a new contract of employment, thousands of State employees failed to report to work on April 1 and 2, 1972. Thereafter, pursuant to the Public Employees' Fair Employment Act (Civil Service Law, art. 14, § 210), New York State's Director of Employee Relations notified approximately 7,800 employees individually that it had been determined that each of them had been illegally on strike, and that, pursuant to the statute, they would be placed on nontenure probationary status for one year, and that they would be fined two days' pay for each day they had been illegally on strike, but that they could file an affidavit within 20 days showing that such determination was incorrect. About 3,400 of the 7,800 did file such affidavits, and the Director of Employee Relations sustained approximately 500 of them and determined that they had not been on strike. The director further determined that 694 of the affidavits had raised questions of fact which would warrant a hearing by a hearing officer. Such hearing officer's evidentiary determination would be judicially reviewable by a proceeding under CPLR article 78. The director further determined that approximately 2,300 of the affidavits were prima facie without merit, but that these 2,300 determinations, too, could be judicially reviewed by proceedings under CPLR article 78. Constitutional due process is satisfied by these statutory procedures and by the judicial reviewability of the determinations.

2. Although a duly notified employee has the burden of producing a prima facie sufficient affidavit of fact, any adverse determination is judicially reversible retroactively and without any irreparable harm to the employee.

People v. Walls


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 419; 321 N.E.2d 875; 363 N.Y.S.2d 82; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1218


November 14, 1974, Argued  
November 18, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: In each case: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decisions of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed their convictions on drug charges.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendants on drug charges and the appellate court affirmed the convictions. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court because it found no merit in defendants' claim that the state lacked the power to prosecute because defendants were apprehended slightly beyond the state's jurisdiction. The court found that although defendants were not returned to the state in compliance with the foreign state statute, the state court was not deprived of jurisdiction. The court also found that the evidence against them should not have been suppressed because it was seized incident to an authorized arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court that affirmed defendants' convictions on drug charges.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- jurisdiction of New York courts -- although defendants, arrested in Lincoln Tunnel beyond New York jurisdiction by New York City officers, were not returned in compliance with New Jersey statute, that did not deprive New York courts of jurisdiction; breach did not call for New York to decline jurisdiction since officers acted in good faith and did not knowingly disregard law -- arrest and incidental search of automobile which followed being valid, evidence should not be suppressed.

1. New York City police officers and a Federal agent had approached defendants to arrest them for possession and attempted sale of narcotics and as one of defendants was apprehended, the other defendants, seated in an automobile, fled toward the Hudson River. Two city police officers pursued and arrested them in the Lincoln Tunnel, the arrest having taken place beyond New York's jurisdiction. Although defendants were not returned to New York in compliance with a New Jersey statute providing for arraignment and extradition, that did not deprive New York courts of jurisdiction. While New York may decline to exercise jurisdiction rather than exploit the fruits of unauthorized conduct, the breach involved does not call for this sanction since the officers acted in good faith and did not knowingly or intentionally disregard the law.

2. The evidence seized should not be suppressed. The arrest and incidental search were valid. The officers reasonably believed they were authorized to act as they did.

Lezette v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 272; 319 N.E.2d 189; 360 N.Y.S.2d 869; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1296


September 12, 1974, Argued  
October 8, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, with costs to petitioner-respondent, in accordance with the opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teacher was hired on a probationary basis and filed an article 78 proceeding against respondent board of education (board) after her position was abolished. The employee sought adjudication that the board's actions were contrary to law and requested an order that she be assigned to a teaching position and receive back pay. The Appellate Division (New York) ordered that the petition be granted, and the board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was hired on a probationary basis to teach first grade. The teacher discovered that her position was being abolished and requested that she be considered for and granted another position. Several positions were available; however, the teacher was not offered a new position. The board admitted that had the teacher's position not been abolished, she would have continued to be employed. On appeal, the court determined that while the teacher's position was abolished, she was never terminated by the board. Pursuant to N.Y. Educ. Law § 2509(1), the superintendent of schools was required to recommend to the board that the teacher be dismissed. The record revealed that no such request was made. Thus, the teacher remained an employee of the school district (district) and as such, was available for another similar position within the district. Further, she was to be given seniority rights over other probationary teachers, substitute teachers, and newly employed teachers whose service was less than hers. Therefore, the teacher had seniority over the teachers newly employed by the board after the date that her position was abolished.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate division was affirmed but modified. The teacher was entitled to be reinstated nunc pro tunc to a teaching position with back salary as granted by the appellate division. However, the board was entitled to a credit for earnings that the teacher may have had from other employment during the period in question, exclusive of summer work.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- teachers -- services of petitioner, probationary teacher, whose position was abolished, were not discontinued since there was no evidence that superintendent of schools recommended such discontinuance or that majority of board of education voted to terminate her services and abolition of her position did not result in termination; accordingly, petitioner continued as employee of board -- petitioner had seniority rights over newly appointed teachers and, therefore, her reinstatment was properly ordered nunc pro tunc -- amicus curiae may properly point out that court may lack jurisdiction because of nonjoinder of newly appointed teachers, but that question of jurisdiction need not be reached.

1. Effective September 1, 1971 petitioner was employed by respondent board of education as a probationary teacher. In June, 1972 petitioner was advised in writing that her position had been abolished, but no mention was made of terminating her employment. Section 2509 (subd. 1) of the Education Law provides that the services of a probationary teacher may be discontinued, on recommendation of the superintendent of schools, by a majority vote of the board and there is no evidence that the superintendent made such a recommendation or that a majority of the board voted to terminate petitioner's services. The abolition of her position did not terminate her services. Reading sections 2509 and 2510 of the Education Law together, the board must take special action to discontinue the services of a teacher whose position has been abolished and, accordingly, petitioner continued as an employee of respondent.

2. Pursuant to the provisions of section 2510 of the Education Law, providing for reappointment in accordance with seniority of teachers whose positions have been abolished, petitioner has limited seniority rights even though she is a probationary teacher. The Commissioner of Education has consistently ruled that section 2510 applies to probationary teachers and that construction is reasonable and is controlling. Petitioner, therefore, had seniority rights over newly appointed teachers and her reinstatement was properly ordered nunc pro tunc as of September 5, 1972.

3. Although an amicus curiae has no status to present new issues, it may properly point out that the court lacks jurisdiction because of the nonjoinder of the newly appointed teachers. However, the status of those teachers being postulated, the question of nonjoinder is not reached.

In re WALTEMADE


STATE OF NEW YORK COURT ON THE JUDICIARY


1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1850



September 19, 1974 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent justice, through his counsel, filed a motion to terminate proceedings against him pursuant to N.Y. Const. art. VI, § 22.


OVERVIEW: The justice faced the imposition of a forfeiture of his elective office because of an alleged violation of a code of conduct and was subject to prohibition from holding future public office. His counsel sought an order vacating and terminating all proceedings had or to be had upon the grounds that the convening of the court violated rights guaranteed to the justice and to the electorate of his district by U.S. Const. V and XIV in that the proceeding required the court to enact ad hoc standards for judicial patterns of conduct unrelated to bribery, corruption, criminality, venality, or willful misconduct because there was no legislative or constitutional mandate for such enactment. His counsel argued that the legislature had the exclusive power to define codes of conduct to be enforced by penal or quasi-penal sanctions and that the court's proceeding imposed ex post facto qualifications upon an elective office. He also argued that the proceeding, insofar as it would determine whether the justice's past conduct warranted his retention in elective office, deprived the electorate of rights granted exclusively to it pursuant to N.Y. Const. art. VI, § 6(c). The court denied the motion.


OUTCOME: The court denied the justice's motion to terminate proceedings against him.

 

51 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Neale v. Hayduk


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 182; 316 N.E.2d 861; 359 N.Y.S.2d 542; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1356


August 27, 1974, Argued  
September 4, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargued September 4, 1974.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, without costs, and judgment granted in favor of appellants declaring sections 187 and 386 of the Election Law to be constitutional insofar as here applicable.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant election board challenged a judgment of the Supreme Court of Westchester County (New York), which, in an action for a declaratory judgment brought by respondent voters, directed the election board to transfer the voters' party enrollment from one county to another and declared N.Y. Elec. Law §§ 187, 386 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The voters were enrolled as democrats in one county. They moved to another county and wished to vote in the upcoming democratic primary, which was to take place four months after their move. The election board informed the voters that they could register for the general election but that they were not eligible to vote in the primary. The voters filed suit, seeking a declaratory judgment directing the election board to transfer the party enrollment of the voters from the first county to the second and to permit them to vote in the primary election. The trial court declared that §§ 187, 386 were unconstitutional in that they denied the voters equal protection by prohibiting or restricting the transfer of enrollments across county lines within the state. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the statutes at issue were not unconstitutional because the legislature had a demonstrable rational basis for the distinction between voters moving from one political subdivision to another and voters moving within the same municipal unit that also happened to lie within another stratum of local government.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the supreme court in favor of the voters and entered a declaration that the election laws at issue were constitutional as applied here.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- enrollment -- section 187 of Election Law, which in effect imposes (subd. 6) waiting period after enrollment as party member of 8 or 11 months before primary election where voter moves from one county to another, but allows (subd. 8) voters to move within City of New York across county lines or within villages straddling two counties to enroll without time delay, is constitutional; it does not deny equal protection since there is rational basis for distinction -- section 386 of Election Law providing for transfer of enrollments is constitutional.

1. Section 186 of the Election Law, which had previously been held valid in Rosario v. Rockefeller (410 U.S. 752) and which provides for a registered voter to enroll as a party member, in effect mandates that people must enroll within 8 or 11 months in advance of a primary election. Section 187 which provides for exceptions to that waiting period but reimposes (subd. 6) that period where a voter moves from one county to another, although it allows (subd. 8) voters who move within the City of New York across county lines or within villages straddling two counties to enroll without time delay at least 30 days prior to a primary election, is constitutional. It does not deny plaintiffs, enrolled Democrats who moved from New York County to Westchester County in May, 1974 and were informed that they could register for the November general election but could not be treated as enrolled Democrats so as to be eligible for the September primary election, equal protection. There is a rational basis for the distinction made by the Legislature between voters moving from one county to another county and those moving within a municipal unit. A transfer of enrollment between unrelated counties involves separate adminstrative units and poses difficulties not found within the same municipal unit.

2. There is no denial of equal protection where the time delay restriction is imposed to preserve the integrity of the various parties.

3. No factual distinction in the instant case warrants a departure from the decision in Matter of Jordan v. Meisser (29 N Y 2d 661, cert. den. 405 U.S. 907) wherein the validity of subdivision 6 of section 187 of the Election Law was upheld over an argument of denial of equal protection.

4. Section 386 of the Election Law providing for the transfer of enrollments is constitutional.

Lutheran Church in America v. New York


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


35 N.Y.2d 121; 316 N.E.2d 305; 359 N.Y.S.2d 7; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1376


May 2, 1974, Argued  
July 15, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order modified, with costs to plaintiff-respondent, in accordance with opinion herein and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of the decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which affirmed a supreme court judgment adjudging that the designation of plaintiff property owner's building as a "landmark" was beyond the power of the Landmarks Preservation Commission and was null and void, and enjoined the city from interfering with the property owner's use of its land and building.


OVERVIEW: The property owner made a case that the building was wholly inadequate for its continued use as office space and that it had to be replaced if the property owner was to be able to freely and economically use the property. The court determined that the city's action through its commission was attempting to force the property owner to retain its property as is, without any sort of relief or adequate compensation, and that this restriction was a taking. Without any move toward invoking the power of eminent domain, the commission was attempting to add the property to the public use by purely and simply invading the owner's right to own and manage. The court determined that the power given the city to force termination of the property owner's free use of its premises short of condemnation directly violated the property owner's rights under the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments and N.Y. Const. art. I, §§ 6, 7. The court concluded that the landmark designation as applied to the premises exceeded the permissible limits of the city's zoning power and it was confiscatory.


OUTCOME: The court modified the appellate court's order to declare that the landmark designation as applied to the property owner's building was confiscatory.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional law -- Landmarks Preservation Law -- former mansion which religious corporation owns and uses for its own offices is wholly inadequate and so corporation wishes to demolish it and erect office building on site; unconstitutional and confiscatory of Landmarks Preservation Commission to forbid this, without compensation for such economic hardship -- in this action for declaratory judgment of unconstitutionality of law as applied to plaintiff, constitutional issue is properly before Court of Appeals, even though courts below improperly converted this action into proceeding for judicial review of reasonableness of commission's designation of landmark.

1. The residential mansion of a famous financier was built in midtown Manhattan in 1853 and was purchased in 1942 by a religious corporation for use for its own offices; however, the building has proved to be wholly inadequate for the religious corporation's purposes and so now the corporation wishes to demolish the mansion and erect a modern office building on the site. But New York City's Landmarks Preservation Commission (Administrative Code of City of New York, ch. 8-A) designates the mansion as an historic landmark and forbids its demolition and replacement. No compensation is provided for this economic hardship to a religious corporation. The Court of Appeals grants judgment declaring that this "landmark designation" amounts to a void and unconstitutional confiscation of the corporation's property (U. S. Const., 5th and 14th Amdts.; N. Y. Const., art. I, §§ 6, 7).

2. Since this is an action for a declaratory judgment of unconstitutionality as applied to plaintiff, and since plaintiff's proof of economic hardship is substantially unchallenged, the constitutional issue is properly before the Court of Appeals for adjudication, even though the courts below improperly converted this declaratory judgment action into a proceeding for judicial review of the reasonableness of the commission's designation of this property as an historic landmark.

 

53 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


Ed Guth Realty, Inc. v. Gingold


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


34 N.Y.2d 440; 315 N.E.2d 441; 358 N.Y.S.2d 367; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1458; 71 A.L.R.3d 224


May 9, 1974, Argued  
June 26, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed, with costs to petitioner.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant realty company and appellant city and its officials (City) each sought review of the decision of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the Fourth Judicial Department (New York) that modified the judgment of the lower court to reduce appellant realty company's property tax assessment. The reduction was made on the basis of the equalization rate that was assessed by the state.


OVERVIEW: In its review of property tax inequality proceedings, the appellate court stated that the equalization rate assessed by the state should be allowed into evidence to prove that the assessed value of the real estate was unequal. Appellant city challenged the use of the state equalization rate as evidence. The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court. The court held that N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 720 (3) (1969) allowed for utilization of the equalization rate in inequality proceedings. The court held that the equalization rate produced a more accurate assessment rate than did evidence of actual sales or selected parcel methods. The court held that the computer records that provided statistical evidence backing up the equalization rate were admissible under the hearsay exception for business records set forth in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 4518.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court that ruled that state equalization assessments could be used as evidence in real estate inequality property tax assessment proceedings. The statistical evidence which was used to show how the equalization assessments were calculated was admissible under the business record exception. Appellant realty company was awarded costs.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- assessments -- inequality -- in reviewing alleged inequality of assessed valuations, court may rely entirely on State equalization rate for 1970 and subsequent years; but as to years 1960 through 1969, State equalization rates may be considered only along with values of selected parcels and actual sales (Real Property Tax Law, § 720, subd. 3) -- both sides may introduce evidence to support or refute State equalization rate -- board's computer printouts admissible ( CPLR 4518) -- property owner was properly awarded reasonable expenses including fees of attorneys (Real Property Tax Law, § 716).

1. In determining whether or not a parcel of real property in the City of Syracuse was assessed unequally, that is, assessed at a higher ratio to its market value than similar properties, the court may, in its judgment as to the assessed valuations for the years 1970 and subsequent years, rely entirely on the applicable State equalization rates; but, as to the assessed valuations for the years 1960 up to and including 1969, the court can only consider the State equalization rates as some evidence along with evidence of the values of selected parcels and evidence of actual sales (Real Property Tax Law, § 720, subd. 3, as amd. by L. 1969, ch. 302).

2. Both the property owner and the taxing authority may introduce testimony and other evidence to support or to refute the weight and relevancy of a State equalization rate.

3. Computer printouts, made by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment, showing data which make up its formulation of the applicable equalization rate, are admissible, as summaries of voluminous records and as entries made in the usual course of business ( CPLR 4518).

4. The property owner was properly awarded reasonable expenses, including fees of experts and attorneys (Real Property Tax Law, § 716).

 

54 of 2939 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cruz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Court of Appeals of New York


34 N.Y.2d 362; 314 N.E.2d 39; 357 N.Y.S.2d 709; 1974 N.Y. LEXIS 1495


May 8, 1974, Argued  
June 13, 1974, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court in the First Judicial Department (New York), which entered an order affirming a judgment of the supreme court rendered upon a verdict convicting defendant of numerous weapons and explosives charges.


OVERVIEW: During the course of defendant's trial for possession and transportation of incendiary bombs, defense counsel alleged that the people were employing information derived from wiretapping of the defendant and defense counsel. The people denied the allegation. On the appeal from affirmance of defendant's conviction, a principal point urged for reversal was that the people's denial was insufficient in law and that a hearing should have been conducted on defendant's allegations. The court held that, on this record, defendant's initial allegation of eavesdropping could only be characterized as vague, conclusory and unsupported. As such, the court held that it barely sufficed to shift to the people the burden of responding. The court held that the people's denial, when coupled with the offer and the court's perusal of the prosecutor's file for traces of eavesdropping evidence, which revealed none, sufficiently met the allegation. Accordingly, the court affirmed the decision of the appellate division.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate division, which affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held that defendant's initial allegation of eavesdropping was vague, conclusory and unsupported.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- eavesdropping -- during trial of defendant for possession and transportation of incendiary bombs and possession of weapon, allegation that People were employing information derived from wiretapping of defendant and defense counsel was vague, conclusory and unsupported and People's denial, coupled with court's perusal of prosecutor's file, sufficiently met allegation -- guidelines with respect to defense allegations of eavesdropping set forth -- arresting officer acted reasonably for his own safety in seizing bag on back seat of automobile in which defendant was passenger -- inculpatory statements of defendant to arresting officer not involuntary.

1. Defendant and another were arrested when the automobile in which they were riding had stopped and was blocking traffic. An officer approached the vehicle and shined his flashlight about the interior of the automobile and noticed a brown bag on the back seat. Thereafter as the officer was returning the license and registration to the driver, defendant who was seated in the front passenger side made a sudden movement toward the brown bag. The officer snatched the bag and defendant shouted, "Be careful man, that's a bomb". The officer then opened the bag and withdrew a device which he recognized to be a bomb mechanism. When asked if the device could detonate, defendant then replied, "if you know anything about bombs, they can't go off." During the course of defendant's trial for possession and transportation of incendiary bombs and possession of a weapon, defense counsel alleged that the People were employing information derived from wiretapping of defendant and defense counsel. The People denied the allegation. That allegation was vague, conclusory and unsupported and barely sufficed to shift to the People the burden of responding. The People's denial, coupled with the court's perusal of the prosecutor's file for traces of eavesdropping evidence, which revealed none, sufficiently met the allegation. Allegations respecting a subsequent cross-examination and a reference in the summation, following so closely upon the previous denial, are within its sweep. These latter allegations were little more than speculative.

2. Defendant has the burden of coming forward with facts which reasonably lead him to believe that he or his counsel had been subjected to undisclosed electronic surveillance. Defendant's allegation should specify, insofar as practicable, the dates of suspected surveillance, the identity of the persons, and the facts relied upon which allegedly link the suspected surveillance to the trial proceedings. It is then incumbent upon the People to affirm or deny the allegations. Ordinarily, a denial should be in affidavit form signed by a responsible officer. The affidavit should specify the law enforcement agencies contacted to determine whether electronic surveillance had occurred, the persons contacted, the substance of the inquiries, and the dates of claimed surveillance. If appropriate, a hearing may be conducted during trial.

3. Given the suspicious circumstances of the traffic stop, the arresting officer acted reasonably for his own safety in seizing the bag. Shining the flashlight about the interior of the automobile was not an unreasonable intrusion and the subsequent search of the automobile at the police station was justifiable.

4. It cannot be said as a matter of law that the inculpatory remarks of defendant to the arresting officer were involuntary.

5. The evidence was sufficient for the jury to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that the device seized was an incendiary bomb containing an explosive substance.

6. The statutory terms, "incendiary", "bomb" and "explosive substance", are susceptible of reasonable application in accordance with the common understanding of men.
